<p><b>Japan</b> (<a href="/wiki/Japanese_language" title="Japanese language">Japanese</a>: <span lang="ja">日本</span>, <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">Nippon</i></span> or <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">Nihon</i></span>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[nb 1]</a></sup> and formally <span title="Japanese-language text"><span lang="ja">日本国</span></span>, <i>Nihonkoku</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fn1_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-fn1-10">[nb 2]</a></sup>) is an <a href="/wiki/Island_country" title="Island country">island country</a> in <a href="/wiki/East_Asia" title="East Asia">East Asia</a>. It is situated in the northwest <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific Ocean</a>, and is bordered on the west by the <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Japan" title="Sea of Japan">Sea of Japan</a>, while extending from the <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Okhotsk" title="Sea of Okhotsk">Sea of Okhotsk</a> in the north toward the <a href="/wiki/East_China_Sea" title="East China Sea">East China Sea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Sea" title="Philippine Sea">Philippine Sea</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a> in the south. Japan is a part of the <a href="/wiki/Ring_of_Fire" title="Ring of Fire">Ring of Fire</a>, and spans <a href="/wiki/Japanese_archipelago" title="Japanese archipelago">an archipelago</a> of <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_of_Japan" title="List of islands of Japan">6852 islands</a> covering 377,975 square kilometers (145,937 sq mi); the five main islands are <a href="/wiki/Hokkaido" title="Hokkaido">Hokkaido</a>, <a href="/wiki/Honshu" title="Honshu">Honshu</a> (the "mainland"), <a href="/wiki/Shikoku" title="Shikoku">Shikoku</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kyushu" title="Kyushu">Kyushu</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Okinawa_Island" title="Okinawa Island">Okinawa</a>. <a href="/wiki/Tokyo" title="Tokyo">Tokyo</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Capital_of_Japan" title="Capital of Japan">nation's capital</a> and largest city, followed by <a href="/wiki/Yokohama" title="Yokohama">Yokohama</a>, <a href="/wiki/Osaka" title="Osaka">Osaka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nagoya" title="Nagoya">Nagoya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sapporo" title="Sapporo">Sapporo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fukuoka" title="Fukuoka">Fukuoka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kobe" title="Kobe">Kobe</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kyoto" title="Kyoto">Kyoto</a>.
</p><p>Japan is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_population" title="List of countries and dependencies by population">eleventh most populous country</a> in the world, as well as one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_population_density" title="List of countries and dependencies by population density">most densely populated</a> and <a href="/wiki/Urbanization_by_country" title="Urbanization by country">urbanized</a>. About three-fourths of <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Japan" title="Geography of Japan">the country's terrain</a> is mountainous, concentrating its population of 125.5 million on narrow <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coastal_plains" title="Coastal plains">coastal plains</a>. Japan is divided into <a href="/wiki/Prefectures_of_Japan" title="Prefectures of Japan">47 administrative prefectures</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_regions_of_Japan" title="List of regions of Japan">eight traditional regions</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Greater_Tokyo_Area" title="Greater Tokyo Area">Greater Tokyo Area</a> is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_cities" title="List of largest cities">most populous metropolitan area</a> in the world, with more than 37.4 million residents.
</p><p>Japan <a href="/wiki/Japanese_Paleolithic" title="Japanese Paleolithic">has been inhabited</a> since the <a href="/wiki/Upper_Paleolithic" title="Upper Paleolithic">Upper Paleolithic</a> period (30,000 BC), though the first written mention of the archipelago appears in a Chinese chronicle (the <i><a href="/wiki/Book_of_Han" title="Book of Han">Book of Han</a></i>) finished in the 2nd century AD. Between the 4th and 9th centuries, the kingdoms of Japan became unified under <a href="/wiki/Emperor_of_Japan" title="Emperor of Japan">an emperor</a> and <a href="/wiki/Imperial_House_of_Japan" title="Imperial House of Japan">the imperial court</a> based in <a href="/wiki/Heian-ky%C5%8D" title="Heian-kyō">Heian-kyō</a>. Beginning in the 12th century, political power was held by a series of military dictators (<span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn"><a href="/wiki/Shogun" title="Shogun">shōgun</a></i></span>) and feudal lords (<span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn"><a href="/wiki/Daimyo" title="Daimyo">daimyō</a></i></span>) and enforced by a class of warrior nobility (<a href="/wiki/Samurai" title="Samurai">samurai</a>). After <a href="/wiki/Sengoku_period" title="Sengoku period">a century-long period of civil war</a>, the country was reunified in 1603 under the <a href="/wiki/Tokugawa_shogunate" title="Tokugawa shogunate">Tokugawa shogunate</a>, which enacted <a href="/wiki/Sakoku" title="Sakoku">an isolationist foreign policy</a>. In 1854, <a href="/wiki/Perry_Expedition" title="Perry Expedition">a United States fleet</a> forced Japan to <a href="/wiki/Bakumatsu" title="Bakumatsu">open trade to the West</a>, which led to <a href="/wiki/Boshin_War" title="Boshin War">the end of the shogunate</a> and <a href="/wiki/Meiji_Restoration" title="Meiji Restoration">the restoration of imperial power</a> in 1868.
</p><p>In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Meiji_(era)" title="Meiji (era)">Meiji period</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Japan" title="Empire of Japan">Empire of Japan</a> adopted <a href="/wiki/Meiji_Constitution" title="Meiji Constitution">a Western-modeled constitution</a> and pursued a program of <a href="/wiki/Industrialisation" title="Industrialisation">industrialization</a> and <a href="/wiki/Modernization_theory" title="Modernization theory">modernization</a>. Amidst a rise in militarism and overseas colonization, Japan <a href="/wiki/Second_Sino-Japanese_War" title="Second Sino-Japanese War">invaded China</a> in 1937 and entered <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> as an <a href="/wiki/Axis_powers" title="Axis powers">Axis power</a> in 1941. After suffering defeat in the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_War" title="Pacific War">Pacific War</a> and <a href="/wiki/Atomic_bombings_of_Hiroshima_and_Nagasaki" title="Atomic bombings of Hiroshima and Nagasaki">two atomic bombings</a>, Japan <a href="/wiki/Surrender_of_Japan" title="Surrender of Japan">surrendered</a> in 1945 and came under a seven-year <a href="/wiki/Occupation_of_Japan" title="Occupation of Japan">Allied occupation</a>, during which it adopted a <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Japan" title="Constitution of Japan">new constitution</a> and began <a href="/wiki/U.S.-Japan_Alliance" title="U.S.-Japan Alliance">a military alliance with the United States</a>. Under the 1947 constitution, Japan has maintained a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">unitary</a> <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentary</a> <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a> with a <a href="/wiki/Bicameralism" title="Bicameralism">bicameral</a> legislature, the <a href="/wiki/National_Diet" title="National Diet">National Diet</a>.
</p><p>Japan is a highly <a href="/wiki/Developed_country" title="Developed country">developed country</a>, and a <a href="/wiki/Great_power" title="Great power">great power</a> in <a href="/wiki/Global_politics" title="Global politics">global politics</a>. Its <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Japan" title="Economy of Japan">economy</a> is the world's <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal)">third-largest by nominal GDP</a> and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP)">fourth-largest by PPP</a>. Although Japan has <a href="/wiki/Article_9_of_the_Japanese_Constitution" title="Article 9 of the Japanese Constitution">renounced its right to declare war</a>, the country maintains <a href="/wiki/Japan_Self-Defense_Forces" title="Japan Self-Defense Forces">Self-Defense Forces</a> that rank as one of the world's strongest militaries. After World War II, Japan experienced record growth in <a href="/wiki/Japanese_economic_miracle" title="Japanese economic miracle">an economic miracle</a>, becoming the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_largest_historical_GDP" title="List of countries by largest historical GDP">second-largest economy</a> in the world by 1972 but has <a href="/wiki/Economic_stagnation" title="Economic stagnation">stagnated</a> since 1995 in what is referred to as the <a href="/wiki/Lost_Decades" title="Lost Decades">Lost Decades</a>. Japan has the world's <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_life_expectancy" title="List of countries by life expectancy">highest life expectancy</a>, though it is experiencing <a href="/wiki/Aging_of_Japan" title="Aging of Japan">a decline in population</a>. A global leader in the <a href="/wiki/Automotive_industry_in_Japan" title="Automotive industry in Japan">automotive</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japanese_robotics" title="Japanese robotics">robotics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Electronics_industry_in_Japan" title="Electronics industry in Japan">electronics industries</a>, the country has made significant contributions to <a href="/wiki/Science_and_technology_in_Japan" title="Science and technology in Japan">science and technology</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Japan" title="Culture of Japan">culture of Japan</a> is well known around the world, including its <a href="/wiki/Japanese_art" title="Japanese art">art</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japanese_cuisine" title="Japanese cuisine">cuisine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Japan" title="Music of Japan">music</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Japanese_popular_culture" title="Japanese popular culture">popular culture</a>, which encompasses prominent <a href="/wiki/Manga" title="Manga">comic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anime" title="Anime">animation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Video_games_in_Japan" title="Video games in Japan">video game</a> industries. It is a member of numerous international organizations, including the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> (since 1956), <a href="/wiki/OECD" title="OECD">OECD</a>, <a href="/wiki/G20" title="G20">G20</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Group_of_Seven" title="Group of Seven">Group of Seven</a>.
</p>
