<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Names_of_Japan" title="Names of Japan">Names of Japan</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066479718" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="infobox"><tbody><tr><th class="infobox-above" colspan="2" style="background-color:#b0c4de">Japan</th></tr><tr style="display:none;"><td class="infobox-full-data" colspan="2"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066479718" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066479718" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/></td></tr><tr><th class="infobox-header" colspan="2" style="background-color: #b0c4de;">Japanese name</th></tr><tr><th class="infobox-label" scope="row" style="font-weight:normal;"><a href="/wiki/Kanji" title="Kanji">Kanji</a></th><td class="infobox-data"><span title="Japanese-language text"><span lang="ja"><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E6%97%A5%E6%9C%AC%E5%9B%BD" title="wikt:日本国">日本国</a></span></span></td></tr><tr><th class="infobox-label" scope="row" style="font-weight:normal;"><a href="/wiki/Hiragana" title="Hiragana">Hiragana</a></th><td class="infobox-data"><span title="Japanese-language text"><span lang="ja"><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E3%81%AB%E3%81%A3%E3%81%BD%E3%82%93%E3%81%93%E3%81%8F" title="wikt:にっぽんこく">にっぽんこく</a><br/><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E3%81%AB%E3%81%BB%E3%82%93%E3%81%93%E3%81%8F" title="wikt:にほんこく">にほんこく</a></span></span></td></tr><tr><th class="infobox-label" scope="row" style="font-weight:normal;"><a href="/wiki/Katakana" title="Katakana">Katakana</a></th><td class="infobox-data"><span title="Japanese-language text"><span lang="ja"><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E3%83%8B%E3%83%83%E3%83%9D%E3%83%B3%E3%82%B3%E3%82%AF" title="wikt:ニッポンコク">ニッポンコク</a><br/><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E3%83%8B%E3%83%9B%E3%83%B3%E3%82%B3%E3%82%AF" title="wikt:ニホンコク">ニホンコク</a></span></span></td></tr><tr><th class="infobox-label" scope="row" style="font-weight:normal;"><a href="/wiki/Ky%C5%ABjitai" title="Kyūjitai">Kyūjitai</a></th><td class="infobox-data"><span title="Japanese-language text"><span lang="ja"><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E6%97%A5%E6%9C%AC%E5%9C%8B" title="wikt:日本國">日本國</a></span></span></td></tr><tr><td class="infobox-full-data" colspan="2"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066479718" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="infobox-subbox collapsible collapsed" style="display:inline-table; text-align: left;"><tbody><tr><th class="infobox-above" colspan="2" style="font-size: 100%; text-align: left; background-color: #f9ffbc;">Transcriptions</th></tr><tr><th class="infobox-label" scope="row" style="font-weight:normal;"><a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Japanese" title="Romanization of Japanese">Romanization</a></th><td class="infobox-data"><span title="Japanese-language romanization"><span lang="ja-Latn" style="font-style: normal">Nippon-koku<br/>Nihon-koku</span></span></td></tr></tbody></table></td><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066479718" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/></tr><tr style="display:none"><td colspan="2">
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The name for Japan in <a href="/wiki/Japanese_language" title="Japanese language">Japanese</a> is written using the <a href="/wiki/Kanji" title="Kanji">kanji</a> <span class="t_nihongo_kanji"><span title="Japanese-language text"><span lang="ja">日本</span></span></span> and is pronounced <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">Nippon</i></span> or <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">Nihon</i></span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-schreiber_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-schreiber-11">[9]</a></sup> Before <span class="t_nihongo_kanji"><span title="Japanese-language text"><span lang="ja">日本</span></span></span> was adopted in the early 8th century, the country was known in China as <span title="Chinese-language romanization"><i lang="zh-Latn"><a href="/wiki/Wa_(Japan)" title="Wa (Japan)">Wa</a></i></span> (<span class="t_nihongo_kanji"><span title="Japanese-language text"><span lang="ja">倭</span></span></span>, changed in Japan around 757 to <span class="t_nihongo_kanji"><span title="Japanese-language text"><span lang="ja">和</span></span></span>) and in Japan by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Endonym" title="Endonym">endonym</a> <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn"><a class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Yamato_(disambiguation)" title="Yamato (disambiguation)">Yamato</a></i></span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-carr_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-carr-12">[10]</a></sup> <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">Nippon</i></span>, the original <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sino-Japanese_reading" title="Sino-Japanese reading">Sino-Japanese reading</a> of the characters, is favored for official uses, including on <a href="/wiki/Japanese_yen" title="Japanese yen">banknotes</a> and postage stamps.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-schreiber_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-schreiber-11">[9]</a></sup> <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">Nihon</i></span> is typically used in everyday speech and reflects shifts in <a href="/wiki/Japanese_phonology" title="Japanese phonology">Japanese phonology</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Edo_period" title="Edo period">Edo period</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-carr_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-carr-12">[10]</a></sup> The characters <span class="t_nihongo_kanji"><span title="Japanese-language text"><span lang="ja">日本</span></span></span> mean "sun origin",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-schreiber_11-2"><a href="#cite_note-schreiber-11">[9]</a></sup> which is the source of the popular Western <a href="/wiki/Epithet" title="Epithet">epithet</a> "Land of the Rising Sun".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[11]</a></sup>
</p><p>The name "Japan" is based on Chinese pronunciations of <span class="t_nihongo_kanji"><span title="Japanese-language text"><span lang="ja">日本</span></span></span> and was introduced to European languages through early trade. In the 13th century, <a href="/wiki/Marco_Polo" title="Marco Polo">Marco Polo</a> recorded the early <a href="/wiki/Mandarin_Chinese" title="Mandarin Chinese">Mandarin</a> or <a href="/wiki/Wu_Chinese" title="Wu Chinese">Wu Chinese</a> pronunciation of the characters <span title="Chinese-language text"><span lang="zh">日本國</span></span> as <span title="Mandarin Chinese-language romanization"><i lang="cmn-Latn">Cipangu</i></span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[12]</a></sup> The old <a href="/wiki/Malay_language" title="Malay language">Malay</a> name for Japan, <span title="Malay (macrolanguage)-language text"><i lang="ms">Japang</i></span> or <span title="Malay (macrolanguage)-language text"><i lang="ms">Japun</i></span>, was borrowed from a southern coastal Chinese dialect and encountered by <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese</a> traders in <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a>, who brought the word to Europe in the early 16th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[13]</a></sup> The first version of the name in English appears in a book published in 1577, which spelled the name as <i>Giapan</i> in a translation of a 1565 Portuguese letter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[15]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Japan" title="History of Japan">History of Japan</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">For a chronological guide, see <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Japanese_history" title="Timeline of Japanese history">Timeline of Japanese history</a>.</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistoric_to_classical_history">Prehistoric to classical history</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Emperor_Jimmu.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1807" data-file-width="1242" decoding="async" height="247" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Emperor_Jimmu.jpg/170px-Emperor_Jimmu.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Emperor_Jimmu.jpg/255px-Emperor_Jimmu.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Emperor_Jimmu.jpg/340px-Emperor_Jimmu.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Emperor_Jimmu.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Legend" title="Legend">Legendary</a> <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Jimmu" title="Emperor Jimmu">Emperor Jimmu</a><span style="font-weight: normal"> (<span title="Japanese-language text"><span lang="ja">神武天皇</span></span>, <span title="Hepburn transliteration"><i lang="ja-Latn">Jinmu-tennō</i></span>)</span></div></div></div>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Japanese_Paleolithic" title="Japanese Paleolithic">Paleolithic culture</a> from around 30,000 BC constitutes the first known habitation of the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_archipelago" title="Japanese archipelago">islands of Japan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[16]</a></sup> This was followed from around 14,500 BC (the start of the <a href="/wiki/J%C5%8Dmon_period" title="Jōmon period">Jōmon period</a>) by a <a href="/wiki/Mesolithic" title="Mesolithic">Mesolithic</a> to <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a> semi-sedentary <a href="/wiki/Hunter-gatherer" title="Hunter-gatherer">hunter-gatherer</a> culture characterized by <a href="/wiki/Pit-house" title="Pit-house">pit dwelling</a> and rudimentary agriculture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[17]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/J%C5%8Dmon_pottery" title="Jōmon pottery">Clay vessels</a> from the period are among the oldest surviving examples of pottery.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[18]</a></sup> From around 700 BC, the <a href="/wiki/Japonic_languages" title="Japonic languages">Japonic</a>-speaking <a href="/wiki/Yayoi_people" title="Yayoi people">Yayoi people</a> began to enter the archipelago from the Korean Peninsula,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yayoi_culture_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-Yayoi_culture-23">[21]</a></sup> intermingling with the <a href="/wiki/J%C5%8Dmon_people" title="Jōmon people">Jōmon</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yayoi_culture_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-Yayoi_culture-23">[21]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Yayoi_period" title="Yayoi period">Yayoi period</a> saw the introduction of practices including <a href="/wiki/Paddy_field" title="Paddy field">wet-rice farming</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[22]</a></sup> a new <a href="/wiki/Yayoi_pottery" title="Yayoi pottery">style of pottery</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[23]</a></sup> and metallurgy from China and Korea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[24]</a></sup> According to legend, <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Jimmu" title="Emperor Jimmu">Emperor Jimmu</a> (grandson of <a href="/wiki/Amaterasu" title="Amaterasu">Amaterasu</a>) founded <a href="/wiki/Yamatai" title="Yamatai">a kingdom</a> in central Japan in 660 BC, beginning a <a href="/wiki/Imperial_House_of_Japan" title="Imperial House of Japan">continuous imperial line</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[25]</a></sup>
</p><p>Japan first appears in written history in the Chinese <i><a href="/wiki/Book_of_Han" title="Book of Han">Book of Han</a></i>, completed in 111 AD. <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a> was introduced to Japan from <a href="/wiki/Baekje" title="Baekje">Baekje</a> (a Korean kingdom) in 552, but the development of <a href="/wiki/Buddhism_in_Japan" title="Buddhism in Japan">Japanese Buddhism</a> was primarily influenced by China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[26]</a></sup> Despite early resistance, Buddhism was promoted by the ruling class, including figures like <a href="/wiki/Prince_Sh%C5%8Dtoku" title="Prince Shōtoku">Prince Shōtoku</a>, and gained widespread acceptance beginning in the <a href="/wiki/Asuka_period" title="Asuka period">Asuka period</a> (592–710).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[27]</a></sup>
</p><p>The far-reaching <a href="/wiki/Taika_Reform" title="Taika Reform">Taika Reforms</a> in 645 nationalized all land in Japan, to be <a href="/wiki/Equal-field_system" title="Equal-field system">distributed equally</a> among cultivators, and ordered the compilation of a household registry as the basis for a new system of taxation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sansom_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sansom-30">[28]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Jinshin_War" title="Jinshin War">Jinshin War</a> of 672, a bloody conflict between <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prince_%C5%8Cama" title="Prince Ōama">Prince Ōama</a> and his nephew <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prince_%C5%8Ctomo" title="Prince Ōtomo">Prince Ōtomo</a>, became a major catalyst for further administrative reforms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ritsuryo_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-ritsuryo-31">[29]</a></sup> These reforms culminated with the promulgation of the <a href="/wiki/Taih%C5%8D_Code" title="Taihō Code">Taihō Code</a>, which consolidated existing statutes and established the structure of the central and subordinate local governments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sansom_30-1"><a href="#cite_note-Sansom-30">[28]</a></sup> These legal reforms created the <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn"><a href="/wiki/Ritsury%C5%8D" title="Ritsuryō">ritsuryō</a></i></span> state, a system of Chinese-style centralized government that remained in place for half a millennium.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ritsuryo_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-ritsuryo-31">[29]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Nara_period" title="Nara period">Nara period</a> (710–784) marked the emergence of a Japanese state centered on the Imperial Court in <a href="/wiki/Heij%C5%8D_Palace" title="Heijō Palace">Heijō-kyō</a> (modern <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nara,_Nara" title="Nara, Nara">Nara</a>). The period is characterized by the appearance of a nascent <a href="/wiki/Japanese_literature" title="Japanese literature">literary culture</a> with the completion of the <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn"><a href="/wiki/Kojiki" title="Kojiki">Kojiki</a></i></span> (712) and <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn"><a href="/wiki/Nihon_Shoki" title="Nihon Shoki">Nihon Shoki</a></i></span> (720), as well as the development of Buddhist-inspired artwork and <a href="/wiki/Historic_Monuments_of_Ancient_Nara" title="Historic Monuments of Ancient Nara">architecture</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Courtiers_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-Courtiers-33">[31]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/735%E2%80%93737_Japanese_smallpox_epidemic" title="735–737 Japanese smallpox epidemic">smallpox epidemic in 735–737</a> is believed to have killed as much as one-third of Japan's population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Courtiers_33-1"><a href="#cite_note-Courtiers-33">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[32]</a></sup> In 784, <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Kanmu" title="Emperor Kanmu">Emperor Kanmu</a> moved the capital, settling on <a href="/wiki/Heian-ky%C5%8D" title="Heian-kyō">Heian-kyō</a> (modern-day <a href="/wiki/Kyoto" title="Kyoto">Kyoto</a>) in 794.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Courtiers_33-2"><a href="#cite_note-Courtiers-33">[31]</a></sup> This marked the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/Heian_period" title="Heian period">Heian period</a> (794–1185), during which a distinctly indigenous Japanese culture emerged. <a href="/wiki/Murasaki_Shikibu" title="Murasaki Shikibu">Murasaki Shikibu</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Tale_of_Genji" title="The Tale of Genji">The Tale of Genji</a></i> and the lyrics of Japan's national anthem <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">"<a href="/wiki/Kimigayo" title="Kimigayo">Kimigayo</a>"</i></span> were written during this time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[33]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Feudal_era">Feudal era</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mokoshuraiekotoba.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="2112" decoding="async" height="107" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Mokoshuraiekotoba.jpg/220px-Mokoshuraiekotoba.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Mokoshuraiekotoba.jpg/330px-Mokoshuraiekotoba.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Mokoshuraiekotoba.jpg/440px-Mokoshuraiekotoba.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mokoshuraiekotoba.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Japanese <a href="/wiki/Samurai" title="Samurai">samurai</a> boarding a Mongol vessel during the <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasions_of_Japan" title="Mongol invasions of Japan">Mongol invasions of Japan</a>, depicted in the <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn"><a href="/wiki/M%C5%8Dko_Sh%C5%ABrai_Ekotoba" title="Mōko Shūrai Ekotoba">Mōko Shūrai Ekotoba</a></i></span>, 1293</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Three_Unifiers_of_Japan.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="748" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/The_Three_Unifiers_of_Japan.jpg/220px-The_Three_Unifiers_of_Japan.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/The_Three_Unifiers_of_Japan.jpg/330px-The_Three_Unifiers_of_Japan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/The_Three_Unifiers_of_Japan.jpg/440px-The_Three_Unifiers_of_Japan.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Three_Unifiers_of_Japan.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Three unifiers of Japan. Left to right: <a href="/wiki/Oda_Nobunaga" title="Oda Nobunaga">Oda Nobunaga</a>, <a href="/wiki/Toyotomi_Hideyoshi" title="Toyotomi Hideyoshi">Toyotomi Hideyoshi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tokugawa_Ieyasu" title="Tokugawa Ieyasu">Tokugawa Ieyasu</a></div></div></div>
<p>Japan's feudal era was characterized by the emergence and dominance of a ruling class of warriors, the <a href="/wiki/Samurai" title="Samurai">samurai</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Leibo2015_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-Leibo2015-36">[34]</a></sup> In 1185, following the defeat of the <a href="/wiki/Taira_clan" title="Taira clan">Taira clan</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Genpei_War" title="Genpei War">Genpei War</a>, samurai <a href="/wiki/Minamoto_no_Yoritomo" title="Minamoto no Yoritomo">Minamoto no Yoritomo</a> established a <a href="/wiki/Military_government" title="Military government">military government</a> at <a href="/wiki/Kamakura" title="Kamakura">Kamakura</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[35]</a></sup> After Yoritomo's death, the <a href="/wiki/H%C5%8Dj%C5%8D_clan" title="Hōjō clan">Hōjō clan</a> came to power as regents for the <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">shōgun</i></span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Courtiers_33-3"><a href="#cite_note-Courtiers-33">[31]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Zen" title="Zen">Zen</a> school of Buddhism was introduced from China in the <a href="/wiki/Kamakura_period" title="Kamakura period">Kamakura period</a> (1185–1333) and became popular among the samurai class.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[36]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Kamakura_shogunate" title="Kamakura shogunate">Kamakura shogunate</a> repelled <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasions_of_Japan" title="Mongol invasions of Japan">Mongol invasions</a> in 1274 and 1281 but was eventually <a href="/wiki/Kenmu_Restoration" title="Kenmu Restoration">overthrown</a> by <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Go-Daigo" title="Emperor Go-Daigo">Emperor Go-Daigo</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Courtiers_33-4"><a href="#cite_note-Courtiers-33">[31]</a></sup> Go-Daigo was defeated by <a href="/wiki/Ashikaga_Takauji" title="Ashikaga Takauji">Ashikaga Takauji</a> in 1336, beginning the <a href="/wiki/Muromachi_period" title="Muromachi period">Muromachi period</a> (1336–1573).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shirane2012a_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-Shirane2012a-39">[37]</a></sup> The succeeding <a href="/wiki/Ashikaga_shogunate" title="Ashikaga shogunate">Ashikaga shogunate</a> failed to control the feudal warlords (<span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">daimyō</i></span>) and a <a href="/wiki/%C5%8Cnin_War" title="Ōnin War">civil war began in 1467</a>, opening the century-long <a href="/wiki/Sengoku_period" title="Sengoku period">Sengoku period</a> ("Warring States").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[38]</a></sup>
</p><p>During the 16th century, Portuguese traders and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jesuit" title="Jesuit">Jesuit</a> missionaries reached Japan for the first time, initiating direct <a href="/wiki/Nanban_trade" title="Nanban trade">commercial</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nanban_art" title="Nanban art">cultural</a> exchange between Japan and the West.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Courtiers_33-5"><a href="#cite_note-Courtiers-33">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[39]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Oda_Nobunaga" title="Oda Nobunaga">Oda Nobunaga</a> used European technology and firearms to conquer many other <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">daimyō</i></span>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[40]</a></sup> his consolidation of power began what was known as the <a href="/wiki/Azuchi%E2%80%93Momoyama_period" title="Azuchi–Momoyama period">Azuchi–Momoyama period</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[41]</a></sup> After <a href="/wiki/Honn%C5%8D-ji_Incident" title="Honnō-ji Incident">the death of Nobunaga</a> in 1582, his successor, <a href="/wiki/Toyotomi_Hideyoshi" title="Toyotomi Hideyoshi">Toyotomi Hideyoshi</a>, unified the nation in the early 1590s and launched <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japanese_invasions_of_Korea_(1592%E2%80%9398)" title="Japanese invasions of Korea (1592–98)">two unsuccessful invasions of Korea in 1592 and 1597</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Courtiers_33-6"><a href="#cite_note-Courtiers-33">[31]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Tokugawa_Ieyasu" title="Tokugawa Ieyasu">Tokugawa Ieyasu</a> served as <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Five_Elders" title="Council of Five Elders">regent</a> for Hideyoshi's son <a href="/wiki/Toyotomi_Hideyori" title="Toyotomi Hideyori">Toyotomi Hideyori</a> and used his position to gain political and military support.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Turnbull2011_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-Turnbull2011-44">[42]</a></sup> When open war broke out, Ieyasu defeated rival clans in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Sekigahara" title="Battle of Sekigahara">Battle of Sekigahara</a> in 1600. He was appointed <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">shōgun</i></span> by <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Go-Y%C5%8Dzei" title="Emperor Go-Yōzei">Emperor Go-Yōzei</a> in 1603 and established the <a href="/wiki/Tokugawa_shogunate" title="Tokugawa shogunate">Tokugawa shogunate</a> at <a href="/wiki/Edo" title="Edo">Edo</a> (modern Tokyo).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Closed_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-Closed-45">[43]</a></sup> The shogunate enacted measures including <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn"><a href="/wiki/Buke_shohatto" title="Buke shohatto">buke shohatto</a></i></span>, as a code of conduct to control the autonomous <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">daimyō</i></span>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[44]</a></sup> and in 1639 the isolationist <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn"><a href="/wiki/Sakoku" title="Sakoku">sakoku</a></i></span> ("closed country") policy that spanned the two and a half centuries of tenuous political unity known as the <a href="/wiki/Edo_period" title="Edo period">Edo period</a> (1603–1868).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Closed_45-1"><a href="#cite_note-Closed-45">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[45]</a></sup> Modern Japan's economic growth began in this period, resulting in <a href="/wiki/Kaid%C5%8D" title="Kaidō">roads</a> and water transportation routes, as well as financial instruments such as <a href="/wiki/Futures_contract" title="Futures contract">futures contracts</a>, banking and insurance of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Osaka_rice_brokers" title="Osaka rice brokers">Osaka rice brokers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[46]</a></sup> The study of Western sciences (<span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn"><a href="/wiki/Rangaku" title="Rangaku">rangaku</a></i></span>) continued through contact with the Dutch enclave in <a href="/wiki/Nagasaki" title="Nagasaki">Nagasaki</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Closed_45-2"><a href="#cite_note-Closed-45">[43]</a></sup> The Edo period gave rise to <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn"><a href="/wiki/Kokugaku" title="Kokugaku">kokugaku</a></i></span> ("national studies"), the study of Japan by the Japanese.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[47]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_era">Modern era</span></h3>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1096954695/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .multiimageinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:312px;max-width:312px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:130px;max-width:130px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:175px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Meiji_tenno1.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1203" data-file-width="879" decoding="async" height="175" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Meiji_tenno1.jpg/128px-Meiji_tenno1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Meiji_tenno1.jpg/192px-Meiji_tenno1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Meiji_tenno1.jpg/256px-Meiji_tenno1.jpg 2x" width="128"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/Emperor_Meiji" title="Emperor Meiji">Emperor Meiji</a><span style="font-weight: normal"> (<span title="Japanese-language text"><span lang="ja">明治天皇</span></span>, <span title="Hepburn transliteration"><i lang="ja-Latn">Meiji-tennō</i></span>)</span>; 1852–1912</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:178px;max-width:178px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:175px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Japanese_Empire_(orthographic_projection).svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="600" decoding="async" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Japanese_Empire_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg/176px-Japanese_Empire_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Japanese_Empire_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg/264px-Japanese_Empire_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Japanese_Empire_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg/352px-Japanese_Empire_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg.png 2x" width="176"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption">The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japanese_Empire" title="Japanese Empire">Japanese Empire</a> in 1942</div></div></div></div></div>
<p>In 1854, Commodore <a href="/wiki/Matthew_C._Perry" title="Matthew C. Perry">Matthew C. Perry</a> and the "<a href="/wiki/Black_Ships" title="Black Ships">Black Ships</a>" of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">United States Navy</a> forced the opening of Japan to the outside world with the <a href="/wiki/Convention_of_Kanagawa" title="Convention of Kanagawa">Convention of Kanagawa</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Closed_45-3"><a href="#cite_note-Closed-45">[43]</a></sup> Subsequent similar treaties with other Western countries brought economic and political crises.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Closed_45-4"><a href="#cite_note-Closed-45">[43]</a></sup> The resignation of the <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">shōgun</i></span> led to the <a href="/wiki/Boshin_War" title="Boshin War">Boshin War</a> and the establishment of a <a href="/wiki/Abolition_of_the_han_system" title="Abolition of the han system">centralized state</a> nominally unified under the emperor (the <a href="/wiki/Meiji_Restoration" title="Meiji Restoration">Meiji Restoration</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[48]</a></sup> Adopting Western political, judicial, and military institutions, the <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_Japan" title="Cabinet of Japan">Cabinet</a> organized the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Privy_Council_(Japan)" title="Privy Council (Japan)">Privy Council</a>, introduced the <a href="/wiki/Meiji_Constitution" title="Meiji Constitution">Meiji Constitution</a> (29 November 1890), and assembled the <a href="/wiki/National_Diet" title="National Diet">Imperial Diet</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-modernnation_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-modernnation-51">[49]</a></sup> During the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Meiji_period" title="Meiji period">Meiji period</a> (1868–1912), the <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Japan" title="Empire of Japan">Empire of Japan</a> emerged as the most developed nation in <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a> and as an industrialized world power that pursued military conflict to expand its sphere of influence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[52]</a></sup> After victories in the <a href="/wiki/First_Sino-Japanese_War" title="First Sino-Japanese War">First Sino-Japanese War</a> (1894–1895) and the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Japanese_War" title="Russo-Japanese War">Russo-Japanese War</a> (1904–1905), Japan gained control of Taiwan, Korea and the southern half of <a href="/wiki/Sakhalin" title="Sakhalin">Sakhalin</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-modernnation_51-1"><a href="#cite_note-modernnation-51">[49]</a></sup> The Japanese population doubled from 35 million in 1873 to 70 million by 1935, with a significant shift to urbanization.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-excesses_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-excesses-57">[55]</a></sup>
</p><p>The early 20th century saw a period of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taish%C5%8D_period" title="Taishō period">Taishō democracy</a> (1912–1926) overshadowed by increasing <a href="/wiki/Expansionism" title="Expansionism">expansionism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Japanese_militarism" title="Japanese militarism">militarization</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[56]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ramesh_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-ramesh-59">[57]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Japan_during_World_War_I" title="Japan during World War I">World War I</a> allowed Japan, which joined the side of the victorious <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_I" title="Allies of World War I">Allies</a>, to capture <a href="/wiki/German_colonial_empire" title="German colonial empire">German possessions</a> in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pacific" title="Pacific">Pacific</a> and in China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ramesh_59-1"><a href="#cite_note-ramesh-59">[57]</a></sup> The 1920s saw a political shift towards <a href="/wiki/Statism_in_Sh%C5%8Dwa_Japan" title="Statism in Shōwa Japan">statism</a>, a period of lawlessness following the 1923 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_Tokyo_Earthquake" title="Great Tokyo Earthquake">Great Tokyo Earthquake</a>, the passing of <a href="/wiki/Peace_Preservation_Law" title="Peace Preservation Law">laws against political dissent</a>, and a series of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/May_15_Incident" title="May 15 Incident">attempted coups</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-excesses_57-1"><a href="#cite_note-excesses-57">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[59]</a></sup> This process accelerated during the 1930s, spawning a number of radical nationalist groups that shared a hostility to liberal democracy and a dedication to expansion in Asia. In 1931, Japan <a href="/wiki/Japanese_invasion_of_Manchuria" title="Japanese invasion of Manchuria">invaded and occupied Manchuria</a>; following <a href="/wiki/Lytton_Report" title="Lytton Report">international condemnation of the occupation</a>, it resigned from the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a> two years later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Inc1945_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-Inc1945-62">[60]</a></sup> In 1936, Japan signed the <a href="/wiki/Anti-Comintern_Pact" title="Anti-Comintern Pact">Anti-Comintern Pact</a> with <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a>; the 1940 <a href="/wiki/Tripartite_Pact" title="Tripartite Pact">Tripartite Pact</a> made it one of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Axis_Powers" title="Axis Powers">Axis Powers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-excesses_57-2"><a href="#cite_note-excesses-57">[55]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mamoru_Shigemitsu_signs_the_Instrument_of_Surrender,_officially_ending_the_Second_World_War.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4594" data-file-width="5738" decoding="async" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Mamoru_Shigemitsu_signs_the_Instrument_of_Surrender%2C_officially_ending_the_Second_World_War.jpg/220px-Mamoru_Shigemitsu_signs_the_Instrument_of_Surrender%2C_officially_ending_the_Second_World_War.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Mamoru_Shigemitsu_signs_the_Instrument_of_Surrender%2C_officially_ending_the_Second_World_War.jpg/330px-Mamoru_Shigemitsu_signs_the_Instrument_of_Surrender%2C_officially_ending_the_Second_World_War.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Mamoru_Shigemitsu_signs_the_Instrument_of_Surrender%2C_officially_ending_the_Second_World_War.jpg/440px-Mamoru_Shigemitsu_signs_the_Instrument_of_Surrender%2C_officially_ending_the_Second_World_War.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mamoru_Shigemitsu_signs_the_Instrument_of_Surrender,_officially_ending_the_Second_World_War.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Japan's imperial ambitions ended on September 2, 1945, with the country's surrender to the Allies.</div></div></div>
<p>The Empire of Japan invaded other parts of China in 1937, precipitating the <a href="/wiki/Second_Sino-Japanese_War" title="Second Sino-Japanese War">Second Sino-Japanese War</a> (1937–1945).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Paine2012_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-Paine2012-63">[61]</a></sup> In 1940, the Empire <a href="/wiki/Japanese_invasion_of_French_Indochina" title="Japanese invasion of French Indochina">invaded French Indochina</a>, after which the United States placed an oil embargo on Japan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-excesses_57-3"><a href="#cite_note-excesses-57">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[62]</a></sup> On December 7–8, 1941, Japanese forces carried out surprise <a href="/wiki/Attack_on_Pearl_Harbor" title="Attack on Pearl Harbor">attacks on Pearl Harbor</a>, as well as on British forces in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_Malaya" title="Battle of Malaya">Malaya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bombing_of_Singapore_(1941)" title="Bombing of Singapore (1941)">Singapore</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Hong_Kong" title="Battle of Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>, among others, beginning <a href="/wiki/Pacific_War" title="Pacific War">World War II in the Pacific</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[63]</a></sup> Throughout areas occupied by Japan during the war, numerous abuses were committed against local inhabitants, with many forced into <a href="/wiki/Comfort_women" title="Comfort women">sexual slavery</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[64]</a></sup> After <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allied</a> victories during the next four years, which culminated in the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_invasion_of_Manchuria" title="Soviet invasion of Manchuria">Soviet invasion of Manchuria</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Atomic_bombings_of_Hiroshima_and_Nagasaki" title="Atomic bombings of Hiroshima and Nagasaki">atomic bombings of Hiroshima and Nagasaki</a> in 1945, Japan agreed to <a href="/wiki/Surrender_of_Japan" title="Surrender of Japan">an unconditional surrender</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[65]</a></sup> The war cost Japan <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Territorial_conquests_of_the_Empire_of_Japan" title="Territorial conquests of the Empire of Japan">its colonies</a> and millions of lives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-excesses_57-4"><a href="#cite_note-excesses-57">[55]</a></sup> The Allies (led by the United States) repatriated millions of <a href="/wiki/Japanese_diaspora" title="Japanese diaspora">Japanese settlers</a> from their former colonies and military camps throughout Asia, largely eliminating the Japanese empire and its influence over the territories it conquered.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-phoenix_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-phoenix-69">[67]</a></sup> The Allies convened the <a href="/wiki/International_Military_Tribunal_for_the_Far_East" title="International Military Tribunal for the Far East">International Military Tribunal for the Far East</a> to prosecute Japanese leaders for <a href="/wiki/Japanese_war_crimes" title="Japanese war crimes">war crimes</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-phoenix_69-1"><a href="#cite_note-phoenix-69">[67]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1947, Japan adopted <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Japan" title="Constitution of Japan">a new constitution</a> emphasizing liberal democratic practices.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-phoenix_69-2"><a href="#cite_note-phoenix-69">[67]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Occupation_of_Japan" title="Occupation of Japan">Allied occupation</a> ended with the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_San_Francisco" title="Treaty of San Francisco">Treaty of San Francisco</a> in 1952,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[68]</a></sup> and Japan was granted membership in the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> in 1956.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-phoenix_69-3"><a href="#cite_note-phoenix-69">[67]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Japanese_economic_miracle" title="Japanese economic miracle">period of record growth</a> propelled Japan to become the second-largest economy in the world;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-phoenix_69-4"><a href="#cite_note-phoenix-69">[67]</a></sup> this ended in the mid-1990s after the popping of an <a href="/wiki/Japanese_asset_price_bubble" title="Japanese asset price bubble">asset price bubble</a>, beginning the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lost_Decade_(Japan)" title="Lost Decade (Japan)">"Lost Decade"</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[69]</a></sup> On March 11, 2011, Japan suffered one of the <a href="/wiki/2011_T%C5%8Dhoku_earthquake_and_tsunami" title="2011 Tōhoku earthquake and tsunami">largest earthquakes in its recorded history</a>, triggering the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fukushima_Daiichi_nuclear_disaster" title="Fukushima Daiichi nuclear disaster">Fukushima Daiichi nuclear disaster</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nytimes-tsunami_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes-tsunami-72">[70]</a></sup> On May 1, 2019, after the historic <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abdication_of_Emperor_Akihito" title="Abdication of Emperor Akihito">abdication of Emperor Akihito</a>, his son <a href="/wiki/Naruhito" title="Naruhito">Naruhito</a> became Emperor, beginning the <a href="/wiki/Reiwa" title="Reiwa">Reiwa</a> era.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[71]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Japan" title="Geography of Japan">Geography of Japan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Geology_of_Japan" title="Geology of Japan">Geology of Japan</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Satellite_View_of_Japan_1999.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2092" data-file-width="1638" decoding="async" height="217" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Satellite_View_of_Japan_1999.jpg/170px-Satellite_View_of_Japan_1999.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Satellite_View_of_Japan_1999.jpg/255px-Satellite_View_of_Japan_1999.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Satellite_View_of_Japan_1999.jpg/340px-Satellite_View_of_Japan_1999.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Satellite_View_of_Japan_1999.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Japanese_archipelago" title="Japanese archipelago">Japanese archipelago</a></div></div></div>
<p>Japan comprises 6852 islands extending along the Pacific coast of Asia. It stretches over 3000 km (1900 mi) northeast–southwest from the <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Okhotsk" title="Sea of Okhotsk">Sea of Okhotsk</a> to the <a href="/wiki/East_China_Sea" title="East China Sea">East China Sea</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-water_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-water-74">[72]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[73]</a></sup> The country's five main islands, from north to south, are <a href="/wiki/Hokkaido" title="Hokkaido">Hokkaido</a>, <a href="/wiki/Honshu" title="Honshu">Honshu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shikoku" title="Shikoku">Shikoku</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kyushu" title="Kyushu">Kyushu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Okinawa_Island" title="Okinawa Island">Okinawa</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[74]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Ryukyu_Islands" title="Ryukyu Islands">Ryukyu Islands</a>, which include Okinawa, are a chain to the south of Kyushu. The <a href="/wiki/Nanp%C5%8D_Islands" title="Nanpō Islands">Nanpō Islands</a> are south and east of the main islands of Japan. Together they are often known as the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_archipelago" title="Japanese archipelago">Japanese archipelago</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[75]</a></sup> As of 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Japan's territory is 377,975.24 km<sup>2</sup> (145,937.06 sq mi).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-area-2019_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-area-2019-1">[1]</a></sup> Japan has the sixth-longest <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_length_of_coastline" title="List of countries by length of coastline">coastline</a> in the world at 29,751 km (18,486 mi). Because of its far-flung outlying islands, Japan has the eighth largest <a href="/wiki/Exclusive_economic_zone_of_Japan" title="Exclusive economic zone of Japan">Exclusive Economic Zone</a> in the world, covering 4,470,000 km<sup>2</sup> (1,730,000 sq mi).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-cia-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[76]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Japanese archipelago is 67% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Forests" title="Forests">forests</a> and 14% agricultural.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[77]</a></sup> The primarily rugged and mountainous terrain is restricted for habitation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[78]</a></sup> Thus the habitable zones, mainly in the coastal areas, have very high population densities: Japan is the 40th <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_population_density" title="List of countries by population density">most densely populated country</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[80]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Honshu" title="Honshu">Honshu</a> has the highest population density at 450 persons/km<sup>2</sup> (1200/sq mi) as of 2010<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, while <a href="/wiki/Hokkaido" title="Hokkaido">Hokkaido</a> has the lowest density of 64.5 persons/km<sup>2</sup> as of 2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JPCensus_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-JPCensus-83">[81]</a></sup> As of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, approximately 0.5% of Japan's total area is <a href="/wiki/Land_reclamation" title="Land reclamation">reclaimed land</a> (<span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">umetatechi</i></span>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[82]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lake_Biwa" title="Lake Biwa">Lake Biwa</a> is an <a href="/wiki/Ancient_lake" title="Ancient lake">ancient lake</a> and the country's largest freshwater lake.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tabata2016_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tabata2016-85">[83]</a></sup>
</p><p>Japan is substantially prone to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Earthquakes" title="Earthquakes">earthquakes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tsunami" title="Tsunami">tsunami</a> and <a href="/wiki/Types_of_volcanic_eruptions" title="Types of volcanic eruptions">volcanic eruptions</a> because of its location along the Pacific Ring of Fire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[84]</a></sup> It has the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_natural_disaster_risk" title="List of countries by natural disaster risk">17th highest natural disaster risk</a> as measured in the 2016 World Risk Index.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wri_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-wri-87">[85]</a></sup> Japan has 111 active volcanoes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[86]</a></sup> Destructive earthquakes, often resulting in tsunami, occur several times each century;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[87]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/1923_Great_Kant%C5%8D_earthquake" title="1923 Great Kantō earthquake">1923 Tokyo earthquake</a> killed over 140,000 people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[88]</a></sup> More recent major quakes are the 1995 <a href="/wiki/Great_Hanshin_earthquake" title="Great Hanshin earthquake">Great Hanshin earthquake</a> and the <a href="/wiki/2011_T%C5%8Dhoku_earthquake_and_tsunami" title="2011 Tōhoku earthquake and tsunami">2011 Tōhoku earthquake</a>, which triggered a large tsunami.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nytimes-tsunami_72-1"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes-tsunami-72">[70]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Japan#Climate" title="Geography of Japan">Geography of Japan § Climate</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chuurei-tou_Fujiyoshida_17025277650_c59733d6ba_o.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3336" data-file-width="5004" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Chuurei-tou_Fujiyoshida_17025277650_c59733d6ba_o.jpg/220px-Chuurei-tou_Fujiyoshida_17025277650_c59733d6ba_o.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Chuurei-tou_Fujiyoshida_17025277650_c59733d6ba_o.jpg/330px-Chuurei-tou_Fujiyoshida_17025277650_c59733d6ba_o.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Chuurei-tou_Fujiyoshida_17025277650_c59733d6ba_o.jpg/440px-Chuurei-tou_Fujiyoshida_17025277650_c59733d6ba_o.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Chuurei-tou_Fujiyoshida_17025277650_c59733d6ba_o.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Mount_Fuji" title="Mount Fuji">Mount Fuji</a> in Spring, view from <a href="/wiki/Arakurayama_Sengen_Park" title="Arakurayama Sengen Park">Arakurayama Sengen Park</a></div></div></div>
<p>The climate of Japan is predominantly temperate but varies greatly from north to south. The northernmost region, Hokkaido, has a <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">humid continental climate</a> with long, cold winters and very warm to cool summers. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Precipitation_(meteorology)" title="Precipitation (meteorology)">Precipitation</a> is not heavy, but the islands usually develop deep snowbanks in the winter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-91">[89]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Japan" title="Sea of Japan">Sea of Japan</a> region on Honshu's west coast, northwest winter winds bring heavy snowfall during winter. In the summer, the region sometimes experiences extremely hot temperatures because of the <a href="/wiki/Foehn_wind" title="Foehn wind">foehn</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[90]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Central_Highland_(Japan)" title="Central Highland (Japan)">Central Highland</a> has a typical inland humid continental climate, with large temperature differences between summer and winter. The mountains of the <a href="/wiki/Ch%C5%ABgoku_region" title="Chūgoku region">Chūgoku</a> and Shikoku regions shelter the <a href="/wiki/Seto_Inland_Sea" title="Seto Inland Sea">Seto Inland Sea</a> from seasonal winds, bringing mild weather year-round.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_91-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-91">[89]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Pacific coast features a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical" title="Humid subtropical">humid subtropical</a> climate that experiences milder winters with occasional snowfall and hot, humid summers because of the southeast seasonal wind. The Ryukyu and Nanpō Islands have a <a href="/wiki/Subtropics" title="Subtropics">subtropical climate</a>, with warm winters and hot summers. Precipitation is very heavy, especially during the rainy season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_91-2"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-91">[89]</a></sup> The main <a href="/wiki/East_Asian_rainy_season" title="East Asian rainy season">rainy season</a> begins in early May in Okinawa, and the rain front gradually moves north. In late summer and early autumn, <a href="/wiki/Typhoon" title="Typhoon">typhoons</a> often bring heavy rain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[91]</a></sup> According to the Environment Ministry, heavy rainfall and increasing temperatures have caused problems in the agricultural industry and elsewhere.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-climatechange_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-climatechange-94">[92]</a></sup> The highest temperature ever measured in Japan, 41.1 °C (106.0 °F), was recorded on July 23, 2018,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[93]</a></sup> and repeated on August 17, 2020.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[94]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity">Biodiversity</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Japan" title="Wildlife of Japan">Wildlife of Japan</a></div>
<p>Japan has nine forest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ecoregions_in_Japan" title="Ecoregions in Japan">ecoregions</a> which reflect the climate and geography of the islands. They range from <a href="/wiki/Tropical_and_subtropical_moist_broadleaf_forests" title="Tropical and subtropical moist broadleaf forests">subtropical moist broadleaf forests</a> in the Ryūkyū and <a href="/wiki/Bonin_Islands" title="Bonin Islands">Bonin Islands</a>, to <a href="/wiki/Temperate_broadleaf_and_mixed_forests" title="Temperate broadleaf and mixed forests">temperate broadleaf and mixed forests</a> in the mild climate regions of the main islands, to <a href="/wiki/Temperate_coniferous_forest" title="Temperate coniferous forest">temperate coniferous forests</a> in the cold, winter portions of the northern islands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[95]</a></sup> Japan has over 90,000 species of <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Japan" title="Wildlife of Japan">wildlife</a> as of 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sakurai2019_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sakurai2019-98">[96]</a></sup> including the <a href="/wiki/Brown_bear" title="Brown bear">brown bear</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_macaque" title="Japanese macaque">Japanese macaque</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_raccoon_dog" title="Japanese raccoon dog">Japanese raccoon dog</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Small_Japanese_field_mouse" title="Small Japanese field mouse">small Japanese field mouse</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_giant_salamander" title="Japanese giant salamander">Japanese giant salamander</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[97]</a></sup>
</p><p>A large network of <a href="/wiki/List_of_national_parks_of_Japan" title="List of national parks of Japan">national parks</a> has been established to protect important areas of flora and fauna as well as 52 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ramsar_sites_in_Japan" title="Ramsar sites in Japan">Ramsar wetland sites</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[98]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[99]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Sites_in_Japan" title="World Heritage Sites in Japan">Four sites</a> have been inscribed on the UNESCO World Heritage List for their outstanding natural value.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unesco1_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-unesco1-102">[100]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environment">Environment</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Environmental_issues_in_Japan" title="Environmental issues in Japan">Environmental issues in Japan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_in_Japan" title="Climate change in Japan">Climate change in Japan</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kongobuji_Koyasan07n3200.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2133" data-file-width="3200" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Kongobuji_Koyasan07n3200.jpg/220px-Kongobuji_Koyasan07n3200.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Kongobuji_Koyasan07n3200.jpg/330px-Kongobuji_Koyasan07n3200.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Kongobuji_Koyasan07n3200.jpg/440px-Kongobuji_Koyasan07n3200.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kongobuji_Koyasan07n3200.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Autumn <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maple_tree" title="Maple tree">maple leaves</a> (<span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Momiji" title="Momiji">momiji</a></i></span>) at <a href="/wiki/Kong%C5%8Dbu-ji" title="Kongōbu-ji">Kongōbu-ji</a> on <a href="/wiki/Mount_K%C5%8Dya" title="Mount Kōya">Mount Kōya</a>, a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a></div></div></div>
<p>In the period of rapid economic growth after World War II, environmental policies were downplayed by the government and industrial corporations; as a result, <a href="/wiki/Four_Big_Pollution_Diseases_of_Japan" title="Four Big Pollution Diseases of Japan">environmental pollution</a> was widespread in the 1950s and 1960s. Responding to rising concern, the government introduced environmental protection laws in 1970.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[101]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/1973_oil_crisis" title="1973 oil crisis">oil crisis in 1973</a> also encouraged the efficient use of energy because of Japan's lack of natural resources.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[102]</a></sup>
</p><p>Japan ranks 20th in the 2018 <a href="/wiki/Environmental_Performance_Index" title="Environmental Performance Index">Environmental Performance Index</a>, which measures a nation's commitment to environmental sustainability.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[103]</a></sup> Japan is the world's fifth largest emitter of <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">carbon dioxide</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-climatechange_94-1"><a href="#cite_note-climatechange-94">[92]</a></sup>  As the host and signatory of the 1997 <a href="/wiki/Kyoto_Protocol" title="Kyoto Protocol">Kyoto Protocol</a>, Japan is under treaty obligation to reduce its carbon dioxide emissions and to take other steps to curb climate change.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[104]</a></sup> In 2020 the government of Japan announced a target of <a href="/wiki/Carbon_neutrality" title="Carbon neutrality">carbon-neutrality</a> by 2050.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[105]</a></sup> Environmental issues include urban air pollution (<a href="/wiki/NOx" title="NOx">NOx</a>, suspended particulate matter, and toxics), <a href="/wiki/Waste_management" title="Waste management">waste management</a>, water <a href="/wiki/Eutrophication" title="Eutrophication">eutrophication</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nature_conservation" title="Nature conservation">nature conservation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_in_Japan" title="Climate change in Japan">climate change</a>, chemical management and international co-operation for conservation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[106]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Japan" title="Government of Japan">Government of Japan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Japan" title="Politics of Japan">Politics of Japan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Law_of_Japan" title="Law of Japan">Law of Japan</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Emperor_Naruhito_and_Empress_Masako_cropped_Emperor_Naruhito_and_Empress_Masako_20191110_1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="522" data-file-width="879" decoding="async" height="131" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Emperor_Naruhito_and_Empress_Masako_cropped_Emperor_Naruhito_and_Empress_Masako_20191110_1.jpg/220px-Emperor_Naruhito_and_Empress_Masako_cropped_Emperor_Naruhito_and_Empress_Masako_20191110_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Emperor_Naruhito_and_Empress_Masako_cropped_Emperor_Naruhito_and_Empress_Masako_20191110_1.jpg/330px-Emperor_Naruhito_and_Empress_Masako_cropped_Emperor_Naruhito_and_Empress_Masako_20191110_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Emperor_Naruhito_and_Empress_Masako_cropped_Emperor_Naruhito_and_Empress_Masako_20191110_1.jpg/440px-Emperor_Naruhito_and_Empress_Masako_cropped_Emperor_Naruhito_and_Empress_Masako_20191110_1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Emperor_Naruhito_and_Empress_Masako_cropped_Emperor_Naruhito_and_Empress_Masako_20191110_1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Emperor_Naruhito" title="Emperor Naruhito">Emperor Naruhito</a>, current head of state, and <a href="/wiki/Empress_Masako" title="Empress Masako">Empress Masako</a> participated in the <a class="extiw" href="https://ja.wikipedia.org/wiki/%E7%A5%9D%E8%B3%80%E5%BE%A1%E5%88%97%E3%81%AE%E5%84%80" title="ja:祝賀御列の儀">Imperial Procession by motorcar after the Ceremony of the Enthronement</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/T%C5%8Dky%C5%8D_Metropolis" title="Tōkyō Metropolis">Tokyo</a> on 10 November 2019.</div></div></div>
<p>Japan is a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">unitary state</a> and <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a> in which the power of the <a href="/wiki/Emperor_of_Japan" title="Emperor of Japan">Emperor</a> is limited to a ceremonial role.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-euparl_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-euparl-109">[107]</a></sup> Executive power is instead wielded by the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Japan" title="Prime Minister of Japan">Prime Minister of Japan</a> and his <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_Japan" title="Cabinet of Japan">Cabinet</a>, whose sovereignty is vested in the Japanese people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Constitution_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-Constitution-110">[108]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Naruhito" title="Naruhito">Naruhito</a> is the Emperor of Japan, having succeeded his father <a href="/wiki/Akihito" title="Akihito">Akihito</a> upon his accession to the <a href="/wiki/Chrysanthemum_Throne" title="Chrysanthemum Throne">Chrysanthemum Throne</a> in 2019.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-euparl_109-1"><a href="#cite_note-euparl-109">[107]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Diet_of_Japan_Kokkai_2009.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1726" data-file-width="2561" decoding="async" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Diet_of_Japan_Kokkai_2009.jpg/220px-Diet_of_Japan_Kokkai_2009.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Diet_of_Japan_Kokkai_2009.jpg/330px-Diet_of_Japan_Kokkai_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Diet_of_Japan_Kokkai_2009.jpg/440px-Diet_of_Japan_Kokkai_2009.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Diet_of_Japan_Kokkai_2009.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/National_Diet_Building" title="National Diet Building">National Diet Building</a></div></div></div>
<p>Japan's legislative organ is the <a href="/wiki/National_Diet" title="National Diet">National Diet</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Bicameralism" title="Bicameralism">bicameral</a> <a href="/wiki/Parliament" title="Parliament">parliament</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-euparl_109-2"><a href="#cite_note-euparl-109">[107]</a></sup> It consists of a lower <a href="/wiki/House_of_Representatives_(Japan)" title="House of Representatives (Japan)">House of Representatives</a> with 465 seats, elected by popular vote every four years or when dissolved, and an upper <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/House_of_Councillors_(Japan)" title="House of Councillors (Japan)">House of Councillors</a> with 245 seats, whose popularly-elected members serve six-year terms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sec_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-sec-111">[109]</a></sup> There is <a href="/wiki/Universal_suffrage" title="Universal suffrage">universal suffrage</a> for adults over 18 years of age,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[110]</a></sup> with a <a href="/wiki/Secret_ballot" title="Secret ballot">secret ballot</a> for all elected offices.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Constitution_110-1"><a href="#cite_note-Constitution-110">[108]</a></sup> The prime minister as the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a> has the power to appoint and dismiss <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ministers_of_State" title="Ministers of State">Ministers of State</a>, and is <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Investiture" title="Imperial Investiture">appointed</a> by the emperor after being designated from among the members of the Diet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sec_111-1"><a href="#cite_note-sec-111">[109]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Fumio_Kishida" title="Fumio Kishida">Fumio Kishida</a> is Japan's prime minister; he took office after winning the <a href="/wiki/2021_Liberal_Democratic_Party_(Japan)_leadership_election" title="2021 Liberal Democratic Party (Japan) leadership election">2021 Liberal Democratic Party leadership election</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[111]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Right-wing_politics" title="Right-wing politics">right-wing</a> <a href="/wiki/Big_tent" title="Big tent">big tent</a> <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Democratic_Party_(Japan)" title="Liberal Democratic Party (Japan)">Liberal Democratic Party</a> has been the <a href="/wiki/Dominant-party_system" title="Dominant-party system">dominant party</a> in the country since the 1950s, often called the <a href="/wiki/1955_System" title="1955 System">1955 System</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[112]</a></sup>
</p><p>Historically influenced by <a href="/wiki/Chinese_law" title="Chinese law">Chinese law</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Law_of_Japan" title="Law of Japan">Japanese legal system</a> developed independently during the Edo period through texts such as <span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn"><a href="/wiki/Kujikata_Osadamegaki" title="Kujikata Osadamegaki">Kujikata Osadamegaki</a></i></span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dean_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-dean-115">[113]</a></sup> Since the late 19th century, the <a href="/wiki/Judicial_system_of_Japan" title="Judicial system of Japan">judicial system</a> has been largely based on the <a href="/wiki/Civil_law_(legal_system)" title="Civil law (legal system)">civil law</a> of Europe, notably Germany. In 1896, Japan established a <a href="/wiki/Civil_code" title="Civil code">civil code</a> based on the German <a href="/wiki/B%C3%BCrgerliches_Gesetzbuch" title="Bürgerliches Gesetzbuch">Bürgerliches Gesetzbuch</a>, which remains in effect with post–World War II modifications.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[114]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Japan" title="Constitution of Japan">Constitution of Japan</a>, adopted in 1947, is the oldest unamended constitution in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-anomalous-constitution_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-anomalous-constitution-117">[115]</a></sup> Statutory law originates in the legislature, and the constitution requires that the emperor promulgate legislation passed by the Diet without giving him the power to oppose legislation. The main body of Japanese statutory law is called the <a href="/wiki/Six_Codes" title="Six Codes">Six Codes</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dean_115-1"><a href="#cite_note-dean-115">[113]</a></sup> Japan's court system is divided into four basic tiers: the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Japan" title="Supreme Court of Japan">Supreme Court</a> and three levels of lower courts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[116]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Japan" title="Administrative divisions of Japan">Administrative divisions of Japan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Prefectures_of_Japan" title="Prefectures of Japan">Prefectures of Japan</a></div>
<p>Japan is divided into <a href="/wiki/Prefectures_of_Japan" title="Prefectures of Japan">47 prefectures</a>, each overseen by an elected <a href="/wiki/Governor_(Japan)" title="Governor (Japan)">governor</a> and legislature.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-euparl_109-3"><a href="#cite_note-euparl-109">[107]</a></sup> In the following table, the prefectures are grouped by <a href="/wiki/List_of_regions_of_Japan" title="List of regions of Japan">region</a>:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[117]</a></sup>
</p>
