<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Japan" title="Foreign relations of Japan">Foreign relations of Japan</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:G7_in_het_Catshuis.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2574" data-file-width="3861" decoding="async" height="173" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/G7_in_het_Catshuis.jpg/260px-G7_in_het_Catshuis.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/G7_in_het_Catshuis.jpg/390px-G7_in_het_Catshuis.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/G7_in_het_Catshuis.jpg/520px-G7_in_het_Catshuis.jpg 2x" width="260"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:G7_in_het_Catshuis.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Japan is a member of both the <a href="/wiki/G7" title="G7">G7</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/G-20_major_economies" title="G-20 major economies">G20</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>A member state of the United Nations since 1956, Japan is one of the <a href="/wiki/G4_nations" title="G4 nations">G4 nations</a> seeking reform of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">Security Council</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[118]</a></sup> Japan is a member of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Group_of_Seven" title="Group of Seven">G7</a>, <a href="/wiki/Asia-Pacific_Economic_Cooperation" title="Asia-Pacific Economic Cooperation">APEC</a>, and "<a href="/wiki/ASEAN_Free_Trade_Area#ASEAN_Plus_Three" title="ASEAN Free Trade Area">ASEAN Plus Three</a>", and is a participant in the <a href="/wiki/East_Asia_Summit" title="East Asia Summit">East Asia Summit</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-terada_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-terada-121">[119]</a></sup> It is the world's fifth largest donor of <a href="/wiki/Official_development_assistance" title="Official development assistance">official development assistance</a>, donating US$9.2 billion in 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[120]</a></sup> In 2019, Japan had the fourth-largest diplomatic network in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[121]</a></sup>
</p><p>Japan has close economic and military relations with the United States, with which it maintains a <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Mutual_Cooperation_and_Security_between_the_United_States_and_Japan" title="Treaty of Mutual Cooperation and Security between the United States and Japan">security alliance</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-us-relations_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-us-relations-124">[122]</a></sup> The United States is a major market for Japanese exports and a major source of Japanese imports, and is committed to defending the country, with military bases in Japan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-us-relations_124-1"><a href="#cite_note-us-relations-124">[122]</a></sup> Japan is also a member of the <a href="/wiki/Quadrilateral_Security_Dialogue" title="Quadrilateral Security Dialogue">Quadrilateral Security Dialogue</a> (more commonly "the Quad"), a multilateral security collaboration reformed in 2017 aiming to limit Chinese influence in the <a href="/wiki/Indo-Pacific" title="Indo-Pacific">Indo-Pacific</a> region, along with the United States, Australia and India, reflecting existing relations and patterns of cooperation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[123]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[124]</a></sup>
</p><p>Japan's relationship with South Korea had historically been strained because of Japan's treatment of Koreans during <a href="/wiki/Korea_under_Japanese_rule" title="Korea under Japanese rule">Japanese colonial rule</a>, particularly over the issue of <a href="/wiki/Comfort_women" title="Comfort women">comfort women</a>. In 2015, Japan agreed to settle the comfort women dispute with South Korea by issuing a formal apology and paying money to the surviving comfort women.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[125]</a></sup> As of 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> Japan is a major importer of Korean music (<a href="/wiki/K-pop" title="K-pop">K-pop</a>), television (<a href="/wiki/Korean_drama" title="Korean drama">K-dramas</a>), and other cultural products.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[126]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[127]</a></sup>
</p><p>Japan is engaged in several territorial disputes with its neighbors. Japan contests Russia's control of the <a href="/wiki/Kuril_Islands_dispute" title="Kuril Islands dispute">Southern Kuril Islands</a>, which were occupied by the Soviet Union in 1945.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[128]</a></sup> South Korea's control of the <a href="/wiki/Liancourt_Rocks" title="Liancourt Rocks">Liancourt Rocks</a> is acknowledged but not accepted as they are claimed by Japan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-takeshima_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-takeshima-131">[129]</a></sup> Japan has strained relations with China and Taiwan over the <a href="/wiki/Senkaku_Islands" title="Senkaku Islands">Senkaku Islands</a> and the status of <a href="/wiki/Okinotorishima" title="Okinotorishima">Okinotorishima</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[130]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Japan_Self-Defense_Forces" title="Japan Self-Defense Forces">Japan Self-Defense Forces</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:US_Navy_051115-N-8492C-125_The_Japan_Maritime_Self-Defense_Force_(JMSDF)_destroyer_JDS_Kongou_(DDG_173)_sails_in_formation_with_other_JMSDF_ships_and_ships_assigned_to_the_USS_Kitty_Hawk_Carrier_Strike_Group.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3008" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/US_Navy_051115-N-8492C-125_The_Japan_Maritime_Self-Defense_Force_%28JMSDF%29_destroyer_JDS_Kongou_%28DDG_173%29_sails_in_formation_with_other_JMSDF_ships_and_ships_assigned_to_the_USS_Kitty_Hawk_Carrier_Strike_Group.jpg/220px-thumbnail.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/US_Navy_051115-N-8492C-125_The_Japan_Maritime_Self-Defense_Force_%28JMSDF%29_destroyer_JDS_Kongou_%28DDG_173%29_sails_in_formation_with_other_JMSDF_ships_and_ships_assigned_to_the_USS_Kitty_Hawk_Carrier_Strike_Group.jpg/330px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/US_Navy_051115-N-8492C-125_The_Japan_Maritime_Self-Defense_Force_%28JMSDF%29_destroyer_JDS_Kongou_%28DDG_173%29_sails_in_formation_with_other_JMSDF_ships_and_ships_assigned_to_the_USS_Kitty_Hawk_Carrier_Strike_Group.jpg/440px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:US_Navy_051115-N-8492C-125_The_Japan_Maritime_Self-Defense_Force_(JMSDF)_destroyer_JDS_Kongou_(DDG_173)_sails_in_formation_with_other_JMSDF_ships_and_ships_assigned_to_the_USS_Kitty_Hawk_Carrier_Strike_Group.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Japan_Maritime_Self-Defense_Force" title="Japan Maritime Self-Defense Force">JMSDF</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kong%C5%8D_class_destroyer" title="Kongō class destroyer"><span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">Kongō</i></span> class destroyer</a></div></div></div>
<p>Japan is the second-highest-ranked Asian country in the 2022 <a href="/wiki/Global_Peace_Index" title="Global Peace Index">Global Peace Index</a>, after <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[131]</a></sup> It spent 1% of its total GDP on its <a href="/wiki/Military_budget" title="Military budget">defence budget</a> in 2020,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[132]</a></sup> and maintains the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_military_expenditures" title="List of countries by military expenditures">ninth-largest military budget</a> in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[133]</a></sup> The country's military (the <a href="/wiki/Japan_Self-Defense_Forces" title="Japan Self-Defense Forces">Japan Self-Defense Forces</a>) is restricted by <a href="/wiki/Article_9_of_the_Japanese_Constitution" title="Article 9 of the Japanese Constitution">Article 9 of the Japanese Constitution</a>, which renounces Japan's right to declare war or use military force in international disputes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[134]</a></sup> The military is governed by the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Defense_(Japan)" title="Ministry of Defense (Japan)">Ministry of Defense</a>, and primarily consists of the <a href="/wiki/Japan_Ground_Self-Defense_Force" title="Japan Ground Self-Defense Force">Japan Ground Self-Defense Force</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Japan_Maritime_Self-Defense_Force" title="Japan Maritime Self-Defense Force">Japan Maritime Self-Defense Force</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Japan_Air_Self-Defense_Force" title="Japan Air Self-Defense Force">Japan Air Self-Defense Force</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Japanese_Iraq_Reconstruction_and_Support_Group" title="Japanese Iraq Reconstruction and Support Group">deployment of troops to Iraq</a> and Afghanistan marked the first overseas use of Japan's military since World War II.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[135]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Japan" title="Government of Japan">Government of Japan</a> has been making changes to its security policy which include the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/National_Security_Council_(Japan)" title="National Security Council (Japan)">National Security Council</a>, the adoption of the National Security Strategy, and the development of the National Defense Program Guidelines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Japan's_Security_Policy_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-Japan's_Security_Policy-138">[136]</a></sup> In May 2014, Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Shinzo_Abe" title="Shinzo Abe">Shinzō Abe</a> said Japan wanted to shed the passiveness it has maintained since the end of World War II and take more responsibility for regional security.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JapanAsia_139-0"><a href="#cite_note-JapanAsia-139">[137]</a></sup> Recent tensions, particularly with North Korea and China, have reignited the debate over the status of the JSDF and its relation to Japanese society.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[138]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[139]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Domestic_law_enforcement">Domestic law enforcement</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Law_enforcement_in_Japan" title="Law enforcement in Japan">Law enforcement in Japan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Crime_in_Japan" title="Crime in Japan">Crime in Japan</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%E8%AD%A6%E8%A6%96%E5%BA%81_-_panoramio.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="5184" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/%E8%AD%A6%E8%A6%96%E5%BA%81_-_panoramio.jpg/220px-%E8%AD%A6%E8%A6%96%E5%BA%81_-_panoramio.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/%E8%AD%A6%E8%A6%96%E5%BA%81_-_panoramio.jpg/330px-%E8%AD%A6%E8%A6%96%E5%BA%81_-_panoramio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/%E8%AD%A6%E8%A6%96%E5%BA%81_-_panoramio.jpg/440px-%E8%AD%A6%E8%A6%96%E5%BA%81_-_panoramio.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%E8%AD%A6%E8%A6%96%E5%BA%81_-_panoramio.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Metropolitan_Police_Department" title="Tokyo Metropolitan Police Department">Tokyo Metropolitan Police Department</a></div></div></div>
<p>Domestic security in Japan is provided mainly by the <a href="/wiki/Prefectural_police_department" title="Prefectural police department">prefectural police departments</a>, under the oversight of the <a href="/wiki/National_Police_Agency_(Japan)" title="National Police Agency (Japan)">National Police Agency</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[140]</a></sup> As the central coordinating body for the Prefectural Police Departments, the National Police Agency is administered by the <a href="/wiki/National_Public_Safety_Commission_(Japan)" title="National Public Safety Commission (Japan)">National Public Safety Commission</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NPA1977-2_143-0"><a href="#cite_note-NPA1977-2-143">[141]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Special_Assault_Team" title="Special Assault Team">Special Assault Team</a> comprises national-level <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Counter-terrorism" title="Counter-terrorism">counter-terrorism</a> tactical units that cooperate with territorial-level <a href="/wiki/Riot_Police_Unit#Specialist_squads" title="Riot Police Unit">Anti-Firearms Squads and Counter-NBC Terrorism Squads</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WP_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-WP-144">[142]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Japan_Coast_Guard" title="Japan Coast Guard">Japan Coast Guard</a> guards territorial waters surrounding Japan and uses surveillance and control countermeasures against smuggling, marine <a href="/wiki/Environmental_crime" title="Environmental crime">environmental crime</a>, poaching, piracy, spy ships, unauthorized foreign fishing vessels, and illegal immigration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[143]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Firearm_and_Sword_Possession_Control_Law" title="Firearm and Sword Possession Control Law">Firearm and Sword Possession Control Law</a> strictly regulates the civilian ownership of guns, swords and other weaponry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[144]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[145]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Office_on_Drugs_and_Crime" title="United Nations Office on Drugs and Crime">United Nations Office on Drugs and Crime</a>, among the member states of the UN that report statistics as of 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the incidence rates of violent crimes such as murder, abduction, sexual violence and robbery are very low in Japan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[146]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[147]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[148]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[149]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Japan" title="Economy of Japan">Economy of Japan</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nakanoshima_Skyscrapers_in_201504_001.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2400" data-file-width="3840" decoding="async" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Nakanoshima_Skyscrapers_in_201504_001.jpg/220px-Nakanoshima_Skyscrapers_in_201504_001.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Nakanoshima_Skyscrapers_in_201504_001.jpg/330px-Nakanoshima_Skyscrapers_in_201504_001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Nakanoshima_Skyscrapers_in_201504_001.jpg/440px-Nakanoshima_Skyscrapers_in_201504_001.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nakanoshima_Skyscrapers_in_201504_001.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Skyscrapers in <a href="/wiki/Nakanoshima" title="Nakanoshima">Nakanoshima</a>, <a href="/wiki/Osaka" title="Osaka">Osaka</a>; a major <a href="/wiki/Financial_centre" title="Financial centre">financial centre</a> in Japan</div></div></div>
<p>Japan has the world's <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal)">third-largest economy</a> by nominal GDP, after that of the United States and China; and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP)">fourth-largest economy</a> by <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">PPP</a>. As of 2020<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Japan's <a href="/wiki/Labor_market_of_Japan" title="Labor market of Japan">labor force</a> is the world's <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_labour_force" title="List of countries by labour force">eighth-largest</a>, and consists of 66.5 million workers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-cia-3">[3]</a></sup> As of 2021<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Japan has a <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_unemployment_rate" title="List of countries by unemployment rate">low unemployment rate</a> of around 2.8%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[150]</a></sup> Its <a href="/wiki/Poverty_in_Japan" title="Poverty in Japan">poverty rate</a> is the second-highest among the G7 nations,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[151]</a></sup> and exceeds 15.7% of the population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[152]</a></sup> Japan has the highest ratio of <a href="/wiki/National_debt_of_Japan" title="National debt of Japan">public debt</a> to GDP among advanced economies,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[153]</a></sup> with national debt estimated to at 248% relative to GDP as of 2022<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[154]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Japanese_yen" title="Japanese yen">Japanese yen</a> is the world's third-largest <a href="/wiki/Reserve_currency" title="Reserve currency">reserve currency</a> after the US dollar and the euro.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[155]</a></sup>
</p><p>Japan was the world's fourth-largest <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_exports" title="List of countries by exports">exporter</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_imports" title="List of countries by imports">importer</a> in 2021.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[156]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[157]</a></sup> Its exports amounted to 15.6% of its total GDP in 2020.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[158]</a></sup> As of 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Japan's main export markets were the United States (19.8 percent) and China (19.1 percent).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sec_111-2"><a href="#cite_note-sec-111">[109]</a></sup> Its main exports are motor vehicles, iron and steel products, semiconductors and auto parts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia_3-3"><a href="#cite_note-cia-3">[3]</a></sup> Japan's main import markets as of 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> were China (23.5 percent), the United States (11 percent), and Australia (6.3 percent).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sec_111-3"><a href="#cite_note-sec-111">[109]</a></sup> Japan's main imports are machinery and equipment, fossil fuels, foodstuffs, chemicals, and raw materials for its industries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sec_111-4"><a href="#cite_note-sec-111">[109]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Japanese variant of capitalism has many distinct features: <a href="/wiki/Keiretsu" title="Keiretsu">keiretsu</a> enterprises are influential, and <a href="/wiki/Permanent_employment" title="Permanent employment">lifetime employment</a> and seniority-based career advancement are common in the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_work_environment" title="Japanese work environment">Japanese work environment</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oecd2008_161-0"><a href="#cite_note-oecd2008-161">[159]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[160]</a></sup> Japan has a large <a href="/wiki/Cooperative" title="Cooperative">cooperative</a> sector, with three of the world's ten largest cooperatives, including the largest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Consumer_cooperative" title="Consumer cooperative">consumer cooperative</a> and the largest <a href="/wiki/Agricultural_cooperative" title="Agricultural cooperative">agricultural cooperative</a> as of 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[161]</a></sup> It ranks highly for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Competition_(companies)" title="Competition (companies)">competitiveness</a> and <a href="/wiki/Economic_freedom" title="Economic freedom">economic freedom</a>. Japan ranked sixth in the <a href="/wiki/Global_Competitiveness_Report" title="Global Competitiveness Report">Global Competitiveness Report</a> in 2019.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[162]</a></sup> It attracted 31.9 million international tourists in 2019,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[163]</a></sup> and was <a href="/wiki/World_Tourism_rankings" title="World Tourism rankings">ranked eleventh</a> in the world in 2019 for inbound tourism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WTOB_166-0"><a href="#cite_note-WTOB-166">[164]</a></sup> The 2021 <i><a href="/wiki/Travel_and_Tourism_Competitiveness_Report" title="Travel and Tourism Competitiveness Report">Travel and Tourism Competitiveness Report</a></i> ranked Japan first in the world out of 117 countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[165]</a></sup> Its international tourism receipts in 2019 amounted to $46.1 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WTOB_166-1"><a href="#cite_note-WTOB-166">[164]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture_and_fishery">Agriculture and fishery</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Agriculture,_forestry,_and_fishing_in_Japan" title="Agriculture, forestry, and fishing in Japan">Agriculture, forestry, and fishing in Japan</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rice_Paddies_In_Aizu,_Japan.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Rice_Paddies_In_Aizu%2C_Japan.JPG/220px-Rice_Paddies_In_Aizu%2C_Japan.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Rice_Paddies_In_Aizu%2C_Japan.JPG/330px-Rice_Paddies_In_Aizu%2C_Japan.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Rice_Paddies_In_Aizu%2C_Japan.JPG/440px-Rice_Paddies_In_Aizu%2C_Japan.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rice_Paddies_In_Aizu,_Japan.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rice_paddy" title="Rice paddy">rice paddy</a> in <a href="/wiki/Aizu" title="Aizu">Aizu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fukushima_Prefecture" title="Fukushima Prefecture">Fukushima Prefecture</a></div></div></div>
<p>The Japanese agricultural sector accounts for about 1.2% of the total country's GDP as of 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sec_111-5"><a href="#cite_note-sec-111">[109]</a></sup> Only 11.5% of Japan's land is suitable for cultivation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[166]</a></sup> Because of this lack of arable land, a system of <a href="/wiki/Terrace_(earthworks)" title="Terrace (earthworks)">terraces</a> is used to farm in small areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Urbanites_Help_Sustain_Japan's_Historic_Rice_Paddy_Terraces_169-0"><a href="#cite_note-Urbanites_Help_Sustain_Japan's_Historic_Rice_Paddy_Terraces-169">[167]</a></sup> This results in one of the world's highest levels of crop yields per unit area, with an agricultural self-sufficiency rate of about 50% as of 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[168]</a></sup> Japan's small agricultural sector is highly subsidized and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Agricultural_Protectionism_in_Japan" title="Agricultural Protectionism in Japan">protected</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[169]</a></sup> There has been a growing concern about farming as farmers are aging with a difficult time finding successors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[170]</a></sup>
</p><p>Japan ranked seventh in the world in <a href="/wiki/Fishing_industry_by_country" title="Fishing industry by country">tonnage of fish caught</a> and captured 3,167,610 metric tons of fish in 2016, down from an annual average of 4,000,000 tons over the previous decade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[171]</a></sup> Japan maintains one of the world's largest fishing fleets and accounts for nearly 15% of the global catch,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia_3-4"><a href="#cite_note-cia-3">[3]</a></sup> prompting critiques that Japan's fishing is leading to depletion in fish stocks such as <a href="/wiki/Tuna" title="Tuna">tuna</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[172]</a></sup> Japan has sparked controversy by supporting commercial <a href="/wiki/Whaling_in_Japan" title="Whaling in Japan">whaling</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[173]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Industry_and_services">Industry and services</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Manufacturing_in_Japan" title="Manufacturing in Japan">Manufacturing in Japan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trade_and_services_in_Japan" title="Trade and services in Japan">Trade and services in Japan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electronics_industry_in_Japan" title="Electronics industry in Japan">Electronics industry in Japan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Automotive_industry_in_Japan" title="Automotive industry in Japan">Automotive industry in Japan</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2017_Toyota_Camry_TRD.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2492" data-file-width="5019" decoding="async" height="109" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/2017_Toyota_Camry_TRD.jpg/220px-2017_Toyota_Camry_TRD.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/2017_Toyota_Camry_TRD.jpg/330px-2017_Toyota_Camry_TRD.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/2017_Toyota_Camry_TRD.jpg/440px-2017_Toyota_Camry_TRD.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2017_Toyota_Camry_TRD.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A plug-in <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_vehicle" title="Hybrid vehicle">hybrid car</a> manufactured by <a href="/wiki/Toyota" title="Toyota">Toyota</a>. Japan is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_motor_vehicle_production" title="List of countries by motor vehicle production">third-largest</a> maker of motor vehicles in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OICA_Production_Statistics_176-0"><a href="#cite_note-OICA_Production_Statistics-176">[174]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Japan has a large industrial capacity and is home to some of the "largest and most technologically advanced producers of motor vehicles, <a href="/wiki/Machine_tool" title="Machine tool">machine tools</a>, steel and nonferrous metals, ships, <a href="/wiki/Chemical_substance" title="Chemical substance">chemical substances</a>, textiles, and <a href="/wiki/Food_processing" title="Food processing">processed foods</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia_3-5"><a href="#cite_note-cia-3">[3]</a></sup> Japan's industrial sector makes up approximately 27.5% of its GDP.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia_3-6"><a href="#cite_note-cia-3">[3]</a></sup> The country's manufacturing output is the third highest in the world as of 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[175]</a></sup>
</p><p>Japan is the third-largest automobile producer in the world as of 2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> and is home to <a href="/wiki/Toyota" title="Toyota">Toyota</a>, the world's largest automobile company.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OICA_Production_Statistics_176-1"><a href="#cite_note-OICA_Production_Statistics-176">[174]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[176]</a></sup> The Japanese shipbuilding industry faces competition from South Korea and China; a 2020 government initiative identified this sector as a target for increasing exports.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[177]</a></sup>
</p><p>Japan's service sector accounts for about 70% of its total economic output as of 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[178]</a></sup> Banking, retail, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transportation_in_Japan" title="Transportation in Japan">transportation</a>, and telecommunications are all major industries, with companies such as Toyota, <a href="/wiki/Mitsubishi_UFJ_Financial_Group" title="Mitsubishi UFJ Financial Group">Mitsubishi UFJ</a>, -<a href="/wiki/Nippon_Telegraph_and_Telephone" title="Nippon Telegraph and Telephone">NTT</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%C3%86ON_(company)" title="ÆON (company)">ÆON</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Softbank" title="Softbank">Softbank</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hitachi" title="Hitachi">Hitachi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Itochu" title="Itochu">Itochu</a> listed as among the largest in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fortune_Global_500_181-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fortune_Global_500-181">[179]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[180]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Science_and_technology">Science and technology</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_science_and_technology_in_Japan" title="History of science and technology in Japan">History of science and technology in Japan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Science_and_technology_in_Japan" title="Science and technology in Japan">Science and technology in Japan</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Video_gaming_in_Japan" title="Video gaming in Japan">Video gaming in Japan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Japanese_inventions_and_discoveries" title="List of Japanese inventions and discoveries">List of Japanese inventions and discoveries</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kibo_PM_and_ELM-PS.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2039" data-file-width="3072" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Kibo_PM_and_ELM-PS.jpg/220px-Kibo_PM_and_ELM-PS.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Kibo_PM_and_ELM-PS.jpg/330px-Kibo_PM_and_ELM-PS.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Kibo_PM_and_ELM-PS.jpg/440px-Kibo_PM_and_ELM-PS.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kibo_PM_and_ELM-PS.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japanese_Experiment_Module" title="Japanese Experiment Module">Japanese Experiment Module</a> (Kibō) at the <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">International Space Station</a></div></div></div>
<p>Japan is a leading nation in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scientific_research" title="Scientific research">scientific research</a>, particularly in the natural sciences and engineering. The country ranks twelfth among the most innovative countries in the 2020 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bloomberg_Innovation_Index" title="Bloomberg Innovation Index">Bloomberg Innovation Index</a> and 13th in the <a href="/wiki/Global_Innovation_Index" title="Global Innovation Index">Global Innovation Index</a> in 2021, up from 15th in 2019.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[181]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[182]</a></sup> Relative to gross domestic product, Japan's <a href="/wiki/Research_and_development" title="Research and development">research and development</a> budget is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_research_and_development_spending" title="List of countries by research and development spending">second highest in the world</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[183]</a></sup> with 867,000 researchers sharing a 19-trillion-yen research and development budget as of 2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[184]</a></sup> The country has produced twenty-two <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel laureates</a> in either physics, chemistry or medicine,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[185]</a></sup> and three <a href="/wiki/Fields_Medal" title="Fields Medal">Fields medalists</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[186]</a></sup>
</p><p>Japan leads the world in <a href="/wiki/Robotics" title="Robotics">robotics</a> production and use, supplying 55% of the world's 2017 total.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[187]</a></sup> Japan has the second highest number of researchers in science and technology per capita in the world with 14 per 1000 employees.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[188]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Japanese consumer electronics industry, once considered the strongest in the world, is in a state of decline as competition arises in countries like South Korea and China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[189]</a></sup> However, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Video_gaming_in_Japan" title="Video gaming in Japan">video gaming in Japan</a> remains a major industry. In 2014, Japan's consumer video game market grossed $9.6 billion, with $5.8 billion coming from mobile gaming.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[190]</a></sup> By 2015, Japan had become the world's fourth largest <a href="/wiki/PC_game" title="PC game">PC game</a> market, behind only <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, and <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[191]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japan_Aerospace_Exploration_Agency" title="Japan Aerospace Exploration Agency">Japan Aerospace Exploration Agency</a> is Japan's national <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Space_agency" title="Space agency">space agency</a>; it conducts space, planetary, and aviation research, and leads development of rockets and satellites.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[192]</a></sup> It is a participant in the <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">International Space Station</a>: the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japanese_Experiment_Module" title="Japanese Experiment Module">Japanese Experiment Module</a> (Kibō) was added to the station during <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">Space Shuttle</a> assembly flights in 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195">[193]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Space_probe" title="Space probe">space probe</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Akatsuki_(spacecraft)" title="Akatsuki (spacecraft)">Akatsuki</a></i> was launched in 2010 and achieved orbit around Venus in 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[194]</a></sup> Japan's plans in <a href="/wiki/Space_exploration" title="Space exploration">space exploration</a> include building a <a href="/wiki/Colonization_of_the_Moon" title="Colonization of the Moon">moon base</a> and landing astronauts by 2030.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[195]</a></sup> In 2007, it launched lunar explorer <a href="/wiki/SELENE" title="SELENE">SELENE</a> (Selenological and Engineering Explorer) from <a href="/wiki/Tanegashima_Space_Center" title="Tanegashima Space Center">Tanegashima Space Center</a>. The largest lunar mission since the <a href="/wiki/Apollo_program" title="Apollo program">Apollo program</a>, its purpose was to gather data on the <a href="/wiki/Moon#Formation" title="Moon">moon's origin and evolution</a>. The explorer entered a lunar orbit on October 4, 2007,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[196]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[197]</a></sup> and was deliberately crashed into the Moon on June 11, 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200"><a href="#cite_note-200">[198]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Japan" title="Transport in Japan">Transport in Japan</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Japan_Airlines,_Boeing_787-9_JA861J_NRT_(19455285040).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3120" data-file-width="4678" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Japan_Airlines%2C_Boeing_787-9_JA861J_NRT_%2819455285040%29.jpg/220px-Japan_Airlines%2C_Boeing_787-9_JA861J_NRT_%2819455285040%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Japan_Airlines%2C_Boeing_787-9_JA861J_NRT_%2819455285040%29.jpg/330px-Japan_Airlines%2C_Boeing_787-9_JA861J_NRT_%2819455285040%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Japan_Airlines%2C_Boeing_787-9_JA861J_NRT_%2819455285040%29.jpg/440px-Japan_Airlines%2C_Boeing_787-9_JA861J_NRT_%2819455285040%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Japan_Airlines,_Boeing_787-9_JA861J_NRT_(19455285040).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Japan_Airlines" title="Japan Airlines">Japan Airlines</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Flag_carrier" title="Flag carrier">flag carrier</a> of Japan</div></div></div>
<p>Japan has invested heavily in transportation infrastructure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201">[199]</a></sup> The country has approximately 1,200,000 kilometers (750,000 miles) of roads made up of 1,000,000 kilometers (620,000 miles) of city, town and village roads, 130,000 kilometers (81,000 miles) of prefectural roads, 54,736 kilometers (34,011 miles) of general national highways and 7641 kilometers (4748 miles) of national <a href="/wiki/Expressways_of_Japan" title="Expressways of Japan">expressways</a> as of 2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202">[200]</a></sup>
</p><p>Since privatization in 1987,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[201]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/List_of_railway_companies_in_Japan" title="List of railway companies in Japan">dozens of Japanese railway companies</a> compete in regional and local passenger transportation markets; major companies include seven <a href="/wiki/Japan_Railways_Group" title="Japan Railways Group">JR</a> enterprises, <a href="/wiki/Kintetsu_Railway" title="Kintetsu Railway">Kintetsu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seibu_Railway" title="Seibu Railway">Seibu Railway</a> and <a href="/wiki/Keio_Corporation" title="Keio Corporation">Keio Corporation</a>. The high-speed <a href="/wiki/Shinkansen" title="Shinkansen">Shinkansen</a> (bullet trains) that connect major cities are known for their safety and punctuality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204">[202]</a></sup>
</p><p>There are 175 airports in Japan as of 2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia_3-7"><a href="#cite_note-cia-3">[3]</a></sup> The largest domestic airport, <a href="/wiki/Haneda_Airport" title="Haneda Airport">Haneda Airport</a> in Tokyo, was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World%27s_busiest_airports_by_passenger_traffic" title="World's busiest airports by passenger traffic">Asia's second-busiest airport</a> in 2019.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205"><a href="#cite_note-205">[203]</a></sup> The Keihin and Hanshin superport hubs are among the largest in the world, at 7.98 and 5.22 million <a href="/wiki/Twenty-foot_equivalent_unit" title="Twenty-foot equivalent unit">TEU</a> respectively as of 2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206"><a href="#cite_note-206">[204]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_Japan" title="Energy in Japan">Energy in Japan</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kashiwazaki-Kariwa_04780017_(8388173865).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2132" data-file-width="2808" decoding="async" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Kashiwazaki-Kariwa_04780017_%288388173865%29.jpg/220px-Kashiwazaki-Kariwa_04780017_%288388173865%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Kashiwazaki-Kariwa_04780017_%288388173865%29.jpg/330px-Kashiwazaki-Kariwa_04780017_%288388173865%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Kashiwazaki-Kariwa_04780017_%288388173865%29.jpg/440px-Kashiwazaki-Kariwa_04780017_%288388173865%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kashiwazaki-Kariwa_04780017_(8388173865).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Kashiwazaki-Kariwa_Nuclear_Power_Plant" title="Kashiwazaki-Kariwa Nuclear Power Plant">Kashiwazaki-Kariwa Nuclear Power Plant</a></div></div></div>
<p>As of 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, 37.1% of energy in Japan was produced from petroleum, 25.1% from coal, 22.4% from natural gas, 3.5% from <a href="/wiki/Hydropower" title="Hydropower">hydropower</a> and 2.8% from <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power_in_Japan" title="Nuclear power in Japan">nuclear power</a>, among other sources. Nuclear power was down from 11.2 percent in 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207">[205]</a></sup> By May 2012 all of the country's nuclear power plants had been taken offline because of ongoing public opposition following the Fukushima Daiichi nuclear disaster in March 2011, though government officials continued to try to sway public opinion in favor of returning at least some to service.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208"><a href="#cite_note-208">[206]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Sendai_Nuclear_Power_Plant" title="Sendai Nuclear Power Plant">Sendai Nuclear Power Plant</a> restarted in 2015,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209"><a href="#cite_note-209">[207]</a></sup> and since then several other nuclear power plants have been restarted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210">[208]</a></sup> Japan lacks significant domestic reserves and has a heavy dependence on <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_oil_imports" title="List of countries by oil imports">imported energy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211">[209]</a></sup> The country has therefore aimed to diversify its sources and maintain high levels of energy efficiency.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212">[210]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Water_supply_and_sanitation">Water supply and sanitation</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Water_supply_and_sanitation_in_Japan" title="Water supply and sanitation in Japan">Water supply and sanitation in Japan</a></div>
<p>Responsibility for the water and sanitation sector is shared between the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Health,_Labour_and_Welfare_(Japan)" title="Ministry of Health, Labour and Welfare (Japan)">Ministry of Health, Labour and Welfare</a>, in charge of water supply for domestic use; the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Land,_Infrastructure,_Transport_and_Tourism_(Japan)" title="Ministry of Land, Infrastructure, Transport and Tourism (Japan)">Ministry of Land, Infrastructure, Transport and Tourism</a>, in charge of water resources development as well as sanitation; the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_the_Environment_(Japan)" title="Ministry of the Environment (Japan)">Ministry of the Environment</a>, in charge of ambient water quality and environmental preservation; and the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Internal_Affairs_and_Communications" title="Ministry of Internal Affairs and Communications">Ministry of Internal Affairs and Communications</a>, in charge of performance benchmarking of utilities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213">[211]</a></sup> Access to an <a href="/wiki/Improved_water_source" title="Improved water source">improved water source</a> is universal in Japan. About 98% of the population receives piped water supply from public utilities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214">[212]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Japan" title="Demographics of Japan">Demographics of Japan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japanese_people" title="Japanese people">Japanese people</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_of_Japan" title="Ethnic groups of Japan">Ethnic groups of Japan</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_metropolitan_areas_in_Japan" title="List of metropolitan areas in Japan">List of metropolitan areas in Japan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Japan" title="List of cities in Japan">List of cities in Japan</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tokyo_from_the_top_of_the_SkyTree.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3598" data-file-width="5999" decoding="async" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Tokyo_from_the_top_of_the_SkyTree.JPG/260px-Tokyo_from_the_top_of_the_SkyTree.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Tokyo_from_the_top_of_the_SkyTree.JPG/390px-Tokyo_from_the_top_of_the_SkyTree.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Tokyo_from_the_top_of_the_SkyTree.JPG/520px-Tokyo_from_the_top_of_the_SkyTree.JPG 2x" width="260"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tokyo_from_the_top_of_the_SkyTree.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>View of Tokyo from the top of the <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Skytree" title="Tokyo Skytree">Tokyo Skytree</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Greater_Tokyo_Area" title="Greater Tokyo Area">Greater Tokyo Area</a> is ranked as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_metropolitan_areas_by_population" title="List of metropolitan areas by population">most populous metropolitan area</a> in the world.</div></div></div>
<p>Japan has a population of 125.4 million, of which 122.8 million are Japanese nationals (2021 estimates).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-November_2020_population_estimate_215-0"><a href="#cite_note-November_2020_population_estimate-215">[213]</a></sup> A small population of foreign residents makes up the remainder.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216"><a href="#cite_note-216">[214]</a></sup> In 2019, 92% of the total Japanese population lived in cities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217"><a href="#cite_note-217">[215]</a></sup> The capital city Tokyo has a population of 13.9 million (2022).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-toukei-metro_218-0"><a href="#cite_note-toukei-metro-218">[216]</a></sup> It is part of the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Tokyo_Area" title="Greater Tokyo Area">Greater Tokyo Area</a>, the biggest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_metropolitan_areas_by_population" title="List of metropolitan areas by population">metropolitan area</a> in the world with 38,140,000 people (2016).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN_Worlds_Cities_219-0"><a href="#cite_note-UN_Worlds_Cities-219">[217]</a></sup> Japan is an ethnically and culturally <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_ranked_by_ethnic_and_cultural_diversity_level" title="List of countries ranked by ethnic and cultural diversity level">homogeneous society</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-220"><a href="#cite_note-220">[218]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_people" title="Japanese people">Japanese people</a> form 98.1% of the country's population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221"><a href="#cite_note-221">[219]</a></sup> Minority ethnic groups in the country include the indigenous <a href="/wiki/Ainu_people" title="Ainu people">Ainu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ryukyuan_people" title="Ryukyuan people">Ryukyuan people</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-222"><a href="#cite_note-222">[220]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Koreans_in_Japan" title="Koreans in Japan">Zainichi Koreans</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-223"><a href="#cite_note-223">[221]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Chinese_people_in_Japan" title="Chinese people in Japan">Chinese</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-224"><a href="#cite_note-224">[222]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Filipinos_in_Japan" title="Filipinos in Japan">Filipinos</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-225"><a href="#cite_note-225">[223]</a></sup> Brazilians mostly <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japanese_Brazilian" title="Japanese Brazilian">of Japanese descent</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-226"><a href="#cite_note-226">[224]</a></sup> and Peruvians mostly <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japanese_Peruvian" title="Japanese Peruvian">of Japanese descent</a> are also among Japan's small minority groups.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-227"><a href="#cite_note-227">[225]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Burakumin" title="Burakumin">Burakumin</a></i> make up a social minority group.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228"><a href="#cite_note-228">[226]</a></sup>
</p><p>Japan is the world's <a href="/wiki/Aging_of_Japan" title="Aging of Japan">fastest aging country</a> and has the highest proportion of <a href="/wiki/Elderly_people_in_Japan" title="Elderly people in Japan">elderly citizens</a> of any country, comprising one-third of its total population;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EUAgeing_229-0"><a href="#cite_note-EUAgeing-229">[227]</a></sup> this is the result of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Post%E2%80%93World_War_II_baby_boom" title="Post–World War II baby boom">post–World War II baby boom</a>, which was followed by an increase in life expectancy and a decrease in <a href="/wiki/Birth_rate" title="Birth rate">birth rates</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-230"><a href="#cite_note-230">[228]</a></sup> Japan has a <a href="/wiki/Total_fertility_rate" title="Total fertility rate">total fertility rate</a> of 1.4, which is below the <a href="/wiki/Sub-replacement_fertility" title="Sub-replacement fertility">replacement rate</a> of 2.1, and is among the <a href="/wiki/List_of_sovereign_states_and_dependencies_by_total_fertility_rate" title="List of sovereign states and dependencies by total fertility rate">world's lowest</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-231"><a href="#cite_note-231">[229]</a></sup> it has a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Median_age" title="Median age">median age</a> of 48.4, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_median_age" title="List of countries by median age">highest in the world</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IMFAgeing_232-0"><a href="#cite_note-IMFAgeing-232">[230]</a></sup> As of 2020<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, over 28.7 percent of the population is over 65, or one in four out of the Japanese population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EUAgeing_229-1"><a href="#cite_note-EUAgeing-229">[227]</a></sup> As a growing number of younger Japanese are not marrying or remaining childless,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Walia_233-0"><a href="#cite_note-Walia-233">[231]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-234"><a href="#cite_note-234">[232]</a></sup> Japan's population is expected to drop to around 88 million by 2065.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EUAgeing_229-2"><a href="#cite_note-EUAgeing-229">[227]</a></sup>
</p><p>The changes in demographic structure have created a number of social issues, particularly a decline in workforce population and increase in the cost of social security benefits.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Walia_233-1"><a href="#cite_note-Walia-233">[231]</a></sup> The government of Japan projects that there will be almost one elderly person for each person of working age by 2060.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IMFAgeing_232-1"><a href="#cite_note-IMFAgeing-232">[230]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_Japan" title="Immigration to Japan">Immigration</a> and birth incentives are sometimes suggested as a solution to provide younger workers to support the nation's aging population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235"><a href="#cite_note-235">[233]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236"><a href="#cite_note-236">[234]</a></sup> On April 1, 2019, Japan's revised immigration law was enacted, protecting the rights of foreign workers to help reduce labor shortages in certain sectors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-237"><a href="#cite_note-237">[235]</a></sup>
</p>
